Tawara Tsuyoshi Defeats Whit Decisively

The Old English General Was Exhausted, and the Japanese Player Handled It Comfortably

(Six to three)

Tawara (Japan) (Six to zero) Whit (England)

(Six to one)

The match between Tawara and Whit was one of the most exciting in the past three days. One was the former Japanese Davis Cup player, and the other was a veteran who had won the Shanghai singles championship for seven consecutive years. The outcome of this group will determine the fate of the two countries, so they exerted all their strength in this match, which was very impressive.

Although Whit ended up in a one-sided situation, it was a fierce battle. Whit is not a weak player after all. He was full of hope before the game. Maxwell's presence in the doubles was to conserve his strength. Tawara's serve was unexpected, and Whit won two consecutive games. His powerful corner shot took the lead, and Tawara also shot with a powerful force, making four consecutive hits. Whit then lost three consecutive games and then regained one game, tying the score at 3-3, but he was gradually becoming tired. Then in the seventh and eighth games, he was completely defeated, and Tawara won the first set 6-3.

His energy was exhausted in this fierce battle. He hoped to make a last-ditch effort, but after the failure, Whit was already showing signs of fatigue and knew that he could not cope. He lost six consecutive games, and in the second set, he was completely defeated. In this set, Whit knew that his corner shots were not effective, so he tried to lure him with soft shots near the net, but he was unable to get the ball over the net many times due to his weakened arm strength.

Why is it that the diagonal forehand and backhand shots of the two men are rarely accurate? Whit's high and low shots, Tawara will have a way to deal with it, to no avail. And Tawara's fierce chop shot, there is no way to answer. However, Whit's beautiful smashes in the third set also won a lot of applause. Whit only won one game in the sixth game. After watching this game, it is said that if you want to win against Tawara, you cannot just rely on shots, you must focus on strategy.

(Six to three)

(Seven to five)

Terk (England) (One to six) Machida (Japan)

(Six to three)

Local News

Chairman Chiang Arrives in Shanghai at 5 AM Yesterday

▲ Personally Escorting Madame Song's Coffin for Burial

▲ Enjoyable Conversation with Madame Sun

▲ Returning to Jiangxi via Nanjing Today

Chairman Chiang of the National Government arrived in Shanghai by special train from Nanjing at 5:30 AM yesterday. He was accompanied only by Chief of the Guard Wang Shihe and over 40 guards. After alighting from the train, Chiang immediately traveled by car to the Song residence on Seymour Road to personally escort the coffin of his mother-in-law, Madame Song, for burial at the International Cemetery. After resting in Shanghai for one night, he is scheduled to return to Nanjing by special train today, and then return to Jiangxi to command the Communist suppression military operations.

Warship Arrives in Nanjing

▲ Chairman Chiang Departed from Jiangxi on the Evening of the 16th

On the 16th, Chairman Chiang departed from Jiangxi on the Chu-class warship Qijie. It arrived in Nanjing at 8:45 PM the night before last. He rested briefly at the headquarters and then took a special train to Shanghai at 11:05 PM that night. It safely arrived at the North Station at 5:31 AM yesterday morning. The special train consisted of four cars. It was previously rumored that he would fly to Shanghai, but because the time was still early, he changed to a special train. Therefore, there was much misunderstanding outside. This newspaper had news of Chairman Chiang's arrival in Shanghai by train in both Nanjing and Shanghai, but it was deleted by the inspectors, so it could not be published.

▲ Tight Security: From around 4 AM yesterday, the North Station was heavily guarded by soldiers and police. The security was unusually tight. Moreover, this news was quite secret beforehand. Therefore, only a few people went to the station to welcome him, including Mayor Zhang, Chief of Staff of the Garrison Headquarters Xu Jinyuan, Deputy Director Jiang Yi, the two Railway Directors Guo Chengen, and National Government Military Counselor Yang Hu.

▲ Paying Respects to Madame Song: After alighting from the train, Chairman Chiang, accompanied by Mayor Zhang, took Xiong Shihui's armored car to the Song residence on Seymour Road at 5:40 AM.

Chairman Chiang ▲ Emerging from the Song Residence, Holding the Funeral Rope (Photographed by this newspaper)

In the hall, he paid his respects to Madame Song's coffin according to Christian rites. When Chiang got out of the car, he was wearing a summer cloth gown, a straw hat, and sunglasses. Although travel-worn and dark-skinned, he was in high spirits. After arriving at the Song residence, he changed into a black cloth robe, black socks, and black shoes. At 6:15 AM, Chiang and Kong Xiangxi, in Kong's car, followed closely behind the hearse. The funeral procession set off from the main gate of the Song residence at 6:30 AM, with Chiang and Kong's car following the hearse directly to the International Cemetery on Hongqiao Road.

▲ Lunch at the Kong Residence: The funeral ended at 9:30 AM. Chairman Chiang and his wife, Kong Xiangxi and his wife, Song Qingling, Song Ziwen, Ziliang, and Zian returned to the Kong residence on Avenue Petain at around 10 AM, where they had lunch.

▲ Chiang-Song Meeting: Chairman Chiang and Madame Sun Yat-sen, Soong Ching-ling, had not seen each other for two years. They met yesterday afternoon and had a pleasant conversation, mentioning various matters. They were particularly united in their desire for peace and national salvation. Madame Sun did not return to her private residence on Rue Moliere until 4:10 PM.

▲ Receiving Guests: After 1 PM yesterday afternoon, Chairman Chiang received several people at the Kong residence, including Vice Minister of the Navy Chen Shaokuan, Chief of Staff of the National Government Zhu Peide, and Mayor Zhang. Foreign Minister Wang and the newly appointed Ambassador to Japan Jiang Zuobin did not visit. Mr. and Mrs. Chiang did not return to their residence on Rue Cardinal Mercier until around 10 PM last night.

▲ Returning to Nanjing Today: Chairman Chiang was originally scheduled to return to Nanjing by night train last night. Over 40 guards had already been sent to the North Station to make arrangements. However, at around 5 PM in the afternoon, the guards were temporarily withdrawn. It was decided that he would stay in Shanghai for one night and return to Nanjing today, before going on to Jiangxi to take command.

Record of Madame Song's Funeral

▲ Thousands of Relatives and Friends Holding the Funeral Rope

▲ Chairman Chiang and Others Displayed Overwhelming Grief

Madame Ni, the mother of the Song family, was buried at the International Cemetery on Hongqiao Road at 9:30 AM yesterday. The hearse was originally scheduled to depart from the Song residence on Seymour Road at 5 AM, so the participating troops and friends and relatives holding the funeral rope gathered at the Song residence in the early dawn. However, because Chairman Chiang arrived in Shanghai to attend the funeral at 5:40 AM yesterday, the departure was changed to 6:30 AM. No flags or superstitious items were used in the procession. The participants holding the funeral rope numbered over a thousand. Plain cars and white horses marked a momentous occasion.

▲ Participating Troops: The military and police forces participating yesterday included a battalion of infantry and military police from the Garrison Headquarters, the entire military band, a company of naval infantry and the entire naval band from the Ministry of the Navy, the entire first detachment of police from the Public Security Bureau, the motorcycle team, the military band, and Chinese and Western patrolmen from the British and French Concessions, as well as detectives from various military and police agencies, totaling no less than five or six hundred people.

▲ Order of Procession: The order of the procession was as follows: (1) Public Security Bureau Motorcycle Team, (2) Flag (Song), (3) Public Security Bureau Band, (4) National Government Decree, (5) Army Troops, (6) National Government Representative Flag, (7) Additional Vehicles, (8) Garrison Headquarters Band, (9) Portrait Vehicle, (10) Naval Infantry, (11) Huier [Benevolence] Orphanage Band and Students, (12) Navy Band, (13) Security Brigade. From the people holding the funeral rope to the family vehicles, they were guarded on both sides, under the command of Director Chen. (14) People holding the funeral rope, various participating groups, and relatives and friends, following in the rope. (15) Hearse. (16) Military Police. (17) Relatives' Vehicles. (18) Guests' Vehicles.

▲ Glimpse of Security: The procession departed from Seymour Road, passed through Nanyang Road, Xiaoshadu Road, Jing'an Temple Road, turned west onto Great Western Road, passed through Zhongshan Road, Hongqiao Road, and arrived at the International Cemetery. Security along the route was particularly tight, but traffic was not completely cut off. The Public Security Bureau's motorcycle team and detectives from the patrol room were the vanguards, patrolling the route. The patrol room was personally commanded by the patrol leader. The procession was commanded by Tang Haian, Superintendent of the Jianghai Customs, and Huang Renlin of the Lixingshe [Society for Encouragement], with Chen Xizeng, Director of the Public Security Bureau, as the overall commander.

▲ Guests Holding the Funeral Rope: Guests holding the funeral rope included He Chengjun, Zhang Zhaohua, He Yaozu, Lian Shenghai, Chu Fucheng, Yang

Sons and Daughters in mourning at the Cemetery

Xingfo, Yu Qiaqing, Zheng Yuxiu, Zhang Qun, Ma Fuxiang, Zhu Peide and his wife, Liu Shangqing, Li Zhaohuan, Hu Mengjia, Wang Zhengting, Rong Zongjing, Zhang Zuobin, Wang Yiting, Du Yuesheng, Huang Jinrong, Ouyang Ju, Chen Shaokuan, Wang Boling, Cai Yuanpei, Zhang Zhuping, and others, as well as foreign guests such as ambassadors and consuls from France, the United States, and Japan, and various merchants, members of the Municipal Council, totaling over a thousand people. In addition, ladies such as Yu Fengzhi, Mrs. Yu Youren, and Mrs. Dai Jitao also personally rode in cars to escort the coffin.

Madame Song's Funeral, white funeral flags and wreaths adorned the hearse

▲ Prayer at the Hall: At 9:10 AM, the hearse and troops arrived at the International Cemetery. All troops, except for the bands, rested at the west end of the front gate of the International Cemetery. Then, the undertaker respectfully carried the elegiac scrolls, National Government orders, National Government plaques, etc., to the central hall of the International Cemetery. Workers carried Madame Song's coffin to the center of the hall for temporary placement. The Song brothers and Ailing, Qingling, and Meiling (all three ladies were wearing black cloth qipaos and black veils) and Chairman Chiang, Minister Kong, etc., stood respectfully in front of the coffin. Pastor Jiang Changchuan presided over the ceremony and held a prayer service for about five minutes. After the ceremony, the Song brothers and sisters and Chairman Chiang, etc., went to the inner room to rest. During the prayer, Ailing, Qingling, and Meiling all wept uncontrollably. Chairman Chiang also repeatedly wiped his eyes with a handkerchief, showing great grief.

▲ Paying Respects Before the Coffin: After the prayer ceremony by the Song family members, Foreign Minister Wang of the National Government, Deputy Finance Ministers Zhang and Li, Deputy Minister Chen Hai, Mayor Zhang, and guests from various agencies and groups stood respectfully in front of the coffin in a semi-circle and bowed three times. Mayor Zhang then gave a speech of thanks and withdrew. Ma Fuxiang, Chairman of the Mongolian and Tibetan Affairs Commission, also came to Shanghai from Nanjing yesterday, rushing to the International Cemetery to stand silently in front of Madame Song's coffin for three minutes before leaving.

▲ Burial: The burial ceremony began at 9:30 AM. The tomb was located to the left of the hall, next to the west side of Mr. Song Yaoru, the father of Minister Song. The grave was five feet deep, with a copper railing on top, tied with leather straps to allow the coffin to be lowered slowly. The bottom of the grave was paved with cement, and the surrounding area was covered with green grass. Ten workers in blue gowns slowly carried the coffin out of the hall. The Song brothers and sisters, Chairman Chiang, Minister Kong, etc., followed behind. After the coffin reached the tomb, it was placed on the pre-set copper frame. Two Republic of China flags were placed on the coffin. After four Westerners from the International Cemetery finished arranging it, Pastor Jiang Changchuan first prayed, and then a Westerner opened the copper railing button, and the straps were slowly lowered, and the coffin also slowly descended. After about three minutes, the Song brothers and sisters, etc., withdrew. Then the craftsmen placed five square stone slabs on top of the grave. After about five minutes, the Song brothers and sisters, Chairman Chiang, Minister Kong, etc., returned to the grave and bowed respectfully three times. After finishing, Chairman Chiang, accompanied by Song Meiling, and Yu Fengzhi, accompanied by Song Qingling, and Kong Xiangxi, accompanied by Song Ailing, drove back to the Song residence on Seymour Road, arriving at only around 10 AM. The participating troops and funeral guests also dispersed. Minister Song and his siblings waited until all the guests had left before returning to their residence.

Upon hearing of the passing of Madame Song, Sun, being Madame Song's eldest grandson, specially sent someone to present a funeral couplet, which read, "Only the great lady supported the nation, her noble deeds will stand forever. With all the maternal uncles capable of becoming pillars of the nation, her feminine virtues are radiant." Amidst the renewed trend towards peace in Guangdong, this has attracted the attention of all circles.

Municipal Social Affairs Bureau Submits Measures to Prevent Food Shortages

▲ Document Submitted to the Municipal Government

The Municipal Social Affairs Bureau, in view of the recent major floods in various places, believes that future food shortages are likely to pose a danger. Shanghai has a dense population, and temporary measures would be costly and ineffective. In accordance with the Municipal Government's instruction to prepare for grain storage, based on a letter from the Municipal Party Department, it has submitted a report on the reasons for the recent rise in grain prices and the measures taken, along with preventive measures for future food shortages, to the Municipal Government for approval. The original text is transcribed below: "Report on the submission of matters: In accordance with your government's instruction No. 9305, briefly approving the Shanghai Special City Executive Committee of the Chinese Kuomintang's letter forwarding the report of the Fourteenth Branch of the Seventh District Party Department, requesting that grain storage be prepared as soon as possible, we hereby issue an order for prompt investigation and reporting, etc. Upon receipt of this, we have investigated that the recent soaring rice prices are due to two reasons: First, the bad weather has reduced the source; second, the reports of disasters in various provinces have caused public anxiety and uncertainty. At this time of year, when the supply is running low and prices are high, due to rain and scarcity, the price surge is a common phenomenon in this city, but it is not as severe as this time. Since the Food Committee investigators reported on the rising rice prices and the Bean and Rice Industry Association reported that the meeting decided to limit the price to a maximum of 17 yuan per picul, we have been taking precautions. On the 11th of this month, the rice price reached 19.5 yuan, and the price limit set by the rice industry could not be maintained. The next morning, the head of the Fourth Section, Feng Liutang, was sent to Zhabei to explain the origin of the price surge, which was entirely due to weather and public sentiment. If the weather clears and the situation remains calm, the price will not continue to rise. However, the city's grain reserves are not large, unlike in the past. There are few boats arriving from downstream, which is not enough to meet urgent needs. Forcibly suppressing the price may hinder the source, and it is difficult to do in practice. Therefore, four measures were decided: (1) Strictly prohibit underground trading and make market prices public. If there is any underground premium pricing, the bureau will send personnel to secretly investigate at any time and instruct the industry associations to report. Once verified, strict penalties will be imposed. (2) The rice price will be based on 17 yuan, but in this disaster-stricken state, the rice price has actually risen to over 20 yuan. The top-quality粳 rice is temporarily allowed to be priced at 18.9 yuan, and the middle and low grades will be priced accordingly, only allowing for price decreases and not increases. The price must return to a maximum price of 17 yuan per picul within one week. (3) The incoming high-quality rice will be fairly distributed by the industry and must not be released for price gouging. If a rice shop wants to purchase a large quantity, it should be dissuaded. (4) The bureau will forward a letter to the railway bureau to request additional vehicles to transport rice to Shanghai. Rice shops should also limit prices to benefit the citizens. According to the merchants on the scene, everyone agreed and was willing to abide by the decision without any changes. The various rice industry groups in the city have been instructed to comply. In recent days, the weather has cleared and the arrival of rice has gradually increased, and the rice market has gradually fallen by more than two yuan. This is a general summary of the bureau's handling of the recent surge in grain prices. However, the extent and severity of the floods in various places this year are rare in recent decades. Rice-producing provinces such as Hunan, Hubei, Anhui, and Jiangxi have little hope for this year's autumn harvest. The difficulties ahead are unknown. The city has a dense population, frequent demand, and is not a rice-producing area. If we do not take precautions early, the danger will be great once the grain reserves are depleted and the source is cut off. To prevent this, we plan to take advantage of the ongoing fundraising period for the warehouse reserve fund. Your chief will periodically convene the captains of the fundraising teams to urge them to proceed and raise 500,000 yuan in advance for disaster preparedness. This is the first measure. In addition, the Disaster Relief Reserve Fund Law has already been promulgated and implemented by the central government. Now that the disaster has occurred in various provinces, the city's food supply will inevitably be affected. Preparations must not be delayed. The city has already secured new tax revenues, so we plan to follow the law from this year onwards and set aside 2% of the city's total revenue in advance for storage, specifically for relief from food shortages and other disasters. This is the second measure. Since this year's autumn harvest is hopeless, the shortage of food and the rise in grain prices next year are inevitable. To prevent this, we plan to order 10,000 tons of foreign rice in advance for a considerable period of time. Please arrange for the city treasury to temporarily advance the deposit for this order. The Jiangsu Provincial Government has already borrowed money to implement this measure, so we can follow suit to avoid digging a well when we are thirsty. This is the third measure. Are the above measures appropriate? We are submitting this report along with the recent handling of the rice price surge and a list of the captains of the warehouse reserve fund fundraising committee to your chief for speedy review and implementation." The captains of the warehouse reserve fund fundraising team are Wang Yiting, Yu Qiaqing, Qian Xinzhi, Wang Xiaolai, Qin Runqing, Hu Mengjia, Wu Zhenxiu, Xu Jiqing, Gu Xinyi, Yuan Ludeng, Yao Zirang, Liu Hongsheng, Shen Lianfang, Yao Mulian, Wang Yansong, Ye Huijun, Lin Kanghou, Zhu Zixiang, Lu Wenshao, Lao Jingxiu, Zhu Wenqi, Sun Baorong, Pan Gongzhan, Tang Naikang, Zhu Hao, Gu Yuguang, Chen Yafu, Chen Tianxi, Pan Hongding, Tang Chengzong, Zhu Zongluo, Yan Enzuo, Hong Lanxiang, Zhu Yinjiang, Li Fusheng, Xu Guannan, Rong Zongjing, Cheng Zhusun, Tang Shoumin, Wu Zhihao, Chen Yiyuan, Lu Bohong, Chen Guangfu, Wu Yunchu, Cai Zengji, Xu Xinliu, Xu Shengchan, Feng Bingnan, Wen Lanting, and Pei Yunqing.

Jiangsu Flood Relief Association Inaugural Meeting Yesterday

▲ Passed the Organizational Outline

▲ Elected Standing Committee Members

The Jiangsu Flood Relief Association held its inaugural meeting yesterday at Renji Hall. Over thirty people attended, including Zhang Gongquan, Wu Yunzhai, Wang Binyan, Di Pingzi, Wang Yiting, Du Yuesheng, Zhu Yinjiang, Gu Xinyi, and Hu Puan.

Page 14

Wang Yiting was elected as the temporary chairman. He first reported the purpose of the meeting and described the disaster situation in detail. Then, Hu Puan, representing Lin Wenqin, delivered a very impassioned speech, stating that Jiangsu Province had suffered successive bandit, drought, and locust disasters, and its vitality had not yet recovered. Now, there is another major flood. According to reports, the heavily affected disaster areas have reached more than fifty counties. The disaster is extremely tragic and rarely seen. The provincial government has already made arrangements to deal with the emergency and allocated 39,000 yuan to establish a temporary emergency relief fund. It has now decided to raise another 100,000 yuan, and each committee member will donate three months of their salary, with lower-ranking officials deducting their salaries according to their grade, to contribute as much as they can. However, the disaster area is too large, and it is hoped that major philanthropists will provide more support. As for the one million treasury bond issue, before it was issued, it had already been decided to borrow and allocate funds from the construction bond project for use. However, government bonds cannot be immediately converted into cash, and it is proposed to ask everyone to help sell them. The fund for these government bonds has a custodial institution and is very reliable. Subsequently, it was publicly decided to ask the financial community to pledge loans and philanthropists to consider distributing them. Cheng Jingsheng reported on the process of organizing the relief association. Wu Yunzhai spoke, saying that relief is a way to deal with emergencies, and he hoped that in the future, before disasters occur, the government and local authorities will cooperate in prevention, rather than "clutching at Buddha's feet when disaster strikes". Everyone was moved. Next, the organizational outline was adopted, and standing committee members were elected. There were many other proposals, and after Wen Lanting proposed that they be handled by the standing committee members and not discussed, everyone agreed. Shortly after, a photograph was taken and the meeting adjourned.

Organizational Outline of the Jiangsu Flood Relief Association: Article 1: The name of this association is the Jiangsu Flood Relief Association. Article 2: The purpose of this association is to specifically investigate and provide relief for the most serious flood disasters in this province. Article 3: This association will publicly elect a number of committee members to handle all affairs. In addition to fifteen standing committee members, the three fundraising directors hired by the provincial relief association will be ex officio standing committee members of this association. The standing committee members will establish three chairman standing committee members to be stationed at the association to be responsible for handling all affairs. A survey and release team will be established, with one director in each county, and an administrative team will be established, with one team leader and one deputy team leader, all of whom will be invited by this association to be impartial individuals with proven relief experience to take on these roles. Other staff members will be hired separately by this association. Article 4: The powers of this association are listed on the left: (A) The standing committee members will carry out all association affairs. (B) The chairman standing committee members will preside over the handling of all daily association affairs. (C) The survey and release teams, with the director of each county directly reporting to this association, will take on the task of surveying and releasing in the disaster area. The surveyors and releasers will be hired by each director themselves. (D) The administrative team leader will assist the chairman standing committee members and the standing committee members in handling all affairs within the association, with separate audit, accounting, documentation, and general affairs sections. The detailed rules will be formulated separately. Article 5: The committee members of this association, as well as the survey and release directors, administrative team leaders, etc., will all be volunteers. Article 6: The meeting date of the standing committee of this association is tentatively set for once a week, and the executive committee meeting will be held once a month. In the event of special matters, temporary meetings may be held, convened by the standing committee members. Article 7: All relief funds of this association, whether publicly allocated or privately donated, will be collected and released on its behalf. Article 8: When the survey and release personnel of this association depart, they should request additional appointments from the provincial relief association and be given appropriate protection by the government. Article 9: After the relief work of this association is completed and a credit record is printed and sent, it will be dissolved. Article 10: Matters not covered in this outline may be corrected at any time.

▲Elected Standing Committee Members Jiangsu Flood Relief Association: Chairman Standing Committee Members: Wang Yiting, Huang Hanzhi, Cheng Jingsheng; Standing Committee Members: Wen Lanting, Du Yuesheng, Zhang Xiaolin, Wang Xiaolai, Zhang Gongquan, Wu Yunzhai, Shi Liangcai, Xi Yunsheng, Hu Bijian, Wang Binyan, Zhang Xiaoliang, Lin Kanghou, Jin Houcheng, Weng Yinchu, Lu Bohong

▲Telegram Seeking Relief To all newspapers and charitable organizations: Jiangsu Province is unfortunate to have suffered another serious disaster. The Huai, Yi, and Si rivers are all flooding simultaneously and uncontrollably. In addition, the Yangtze River tide is surging, and the lake waters are roaring. All areas along the Yangtze River, the canal, and the coast, spanning more than a thousand li, cannot escape its poisonous effects. Crops are submerged, and people and animals are washed away. The good fields of the past have now become lakes. The most tragic areas, such as Jiangpu, Huai'an, Gaoyou, Baoying, Xinghua, and Xuzhou, etc., more than twenty counties, the affected victims have nowhere to live and often sleep in the open on higher dikes or climb trees and build nests with wood at the mouths of dikes, swaying in the wind and rain without any way to call for help. Even the higher dikes are broken by the fierce wind, and the precarious nests are incomplete. If they avoid it a little late, they will die immediately. Or the child is already dead and goes into the water with it, and the parents are washed away and martyred at the same time. The sound of crying reaches several li away. Those who barely survive suffer from hunger and cannot bear to scavenge for fish and shrimp. Fish and shrimp are hard to find, so they are followed by other aquatic animals, swallowed alive, regardless of toxic substances. Many people die from poisoning in the following days. If emergency relief is not carried out quickly, more shelters are not set up, dry food is not prepared, and effective relief is not provided, deaths will continue to occur day by day. This will not only damage the nation's vitality, but also, in terms of the supreme virtue of cherishing life and the righteousness of human mutual assistance, how can we bear to remain indifferent and unmoved? Our association has gathered like-minded people to work hard to plan and maintain. We respectfully request people who have a reputation for providing relief to go to the disaster area to try their best to rescue. However, the disaster area is too large, and there are too many victims. Our strength is insufficient, and our heart is surplus, making it difficult to provide universal relief. We humbly hope that your benevolence will be widely bestowed and that you will generously agree to assist. Millions of surviving people will all be grateful for your gift. Jiangsu Flood Relief Association: Chairman Standing Committee Members: Wang Yiting, Huang Hanzhi, Cheng Jingsheng; Standing Committee Members: Wen Lanting, Du Yuesheng, Zhang Xiaolin, Wang Xiaolai, Zhang Gongquan, Wu Yunzhai, Shi Liangcai, Xi Yunsheng, Hu Bijian, Wang Binyan, Zhang Xiaoliang, Lin Kanghou, Jin Houcheng, Weng Yinchu, Lu Bohong, respectfully announce.

Japanese Soldiers Again Cross the Border to Rob Goods

Police Intercept Ineffectively

At around 4 PM yesterday, the inspectors of the Zhabei Inspection Department of the Anti-Japanese Aid Overseas Chinese Association seized four large packages of Japanese yarn on a small cart at the intersection of Yokohama Road and Yinggui Road. They immediately seized it and sent it to the warehouse for safekeeping. Unexpectedly, while traveling near the Commercial Press of Baoshan Road, the Japanese Marines at the end of Douleau Road suddenly dispatched a truck with more than ten soldiers, led by an officer, who rushed to the scene to transport the Japanese goods back. A major dispute arose with the inspectors. The police chief of the Shiqing Road Police Station of the Fifth District Public Security Bureau heard the news and, fearing that it would cause trouble, immediately led experienced police officers to suppress and resolve the situation, intending to send the goods to the district office temporarily. However, the Japanese soldiers were extremely barbaric and forcibly snatched the cotton yarn onto the truck and drove away. The police officers who got on the truck to stop them were all pushed down. It was reported that the Japanese officers were all armed at the time.

German Ship Sinks the Xin Hailong

Three People Tragically Drowned

The Xin Hailong, a dredger belonging to the Dredging Bureau, has been dredging the sludge at the mouth of the Bailong Port in the Puxi area opposite Zhanghuabang in Wusong for the past few days, following the orders of the bureau's engineer. The chief of the dredger, Li Jinsheng, had a total of twenty-four people on board, including seventeen machinists, three stokers, one night watchman, and two cooks. The dredger was docked near the Asia Petroleum Company pier a few days ago because the area was a major waterway. Therefore, after dark, three red lights were hung at the front and rear of the ship as a marker to allow other ships to give way. At around 4 AM yesterday morning, when the sky was not yet dawn, everyone on board was lying on the deck because of the hot weather, still in the land of sleep. Unexpectedly, at this time, the Coblenz, a ship belonging to the North German Company, entered the port and sailed to the dredger's mooring place. Due to a slight negligence in navigation, the bow of the ship crashed straight into the dredger. A barge was parked in front of the dredger, and the bow of the ship bore the brunt of the impact and was immediately cut off. The dredger's entire body was made of iron, and its outer barrier was also smashed into a large hole. River water immediately poured in, and the dredger tilted towards the outer barrier and sank to the bottom of the river in an instant. Everyone on board was awakened by the violent tremor, and they were at a loss for a while. Zhou Aisheng, a stoker, saw that the situation was critical and quickly jumped down, shouting for help. However, the dredger sank very quickly, and Zhou did not have time to escape from the deck. Gu Heshang, a machinist, and Pan Agui, a night watchman, also sank to the bottom of the river with the ship and died tragically. The remaining twenty-one people, including Chief Li Jinsheng, heard the news and rushed to take everyone on board the German ship and sent them to Wusong to disembark. After causing the accident, the German merchant ship suffered only minor damage to its bow, but there was no major problem. It then sailed to Shanghai. It is reported that the Xin Hailong dredger was worth more than 300,000 yuan. Chief Li Jinsheng immediately reported to the bureau after the accident. The bureau is now starting to negotiate with the German merchant ship. The deceased Zhou Aisheng was 32 years old, Gu Heshang was 44 years old, and Pan Agui was 35 years old. All were natives of Wusong. Family members were informed of the bad news and were weeping bitterly by the river, which was unbearable to hear. They have already sent representatives to the bureau to request relief and are trying to salvage the bodies. As of yesterday afternoon, the bodies had not yet been recovered.

Wuhan Flood Causes Huge Losses to Shanghai Financial Circles

It has been nearly twenty days since the flooding in Hankou, and the water volume has been increasing recently. Except for food, all other transportation has been suspended. The magnitude of the losses in Wuhan and its surrounding towns this time is incalculable and is truly a great tragedy unprecedented in history. According to news from the financial circles of Shanghai yesterday, the various transactions and financial interactions between Shanghai and Hankou are quite considerable. Now that Hankou has suffered such huge losses, Shanghai's financial circles are bearing the brunt of the impact. Therefore, all sectors related to Hankou are currently looking worried.

Important Proposals from Li Zushen of the Flood Relief Emergency Committee

The Shanghai Flood Relief Emergency Committee discussed its course of action the day before. The important proposals of Zhang Zhuping, Huang Yanpei, Hong Yanbin, Chu Huiseng, Wu Zhihao, Yu Daxiong, etc., were recorded in yesterday's newspaper. Now, it has been learned that the proposals of Li Zushen, a standing committee member of the committee, are also quite important and are supplemented as follows: (1) In areas that have not been affected by the disaster or have been lightly affected, the local government should, in conjunction with charitable organizations, investigate wide houses such as temples, shrines, and churches, and estimate the number of people each can accommodate and consult with them to allow compatriots from disaster areas that have been seriously affected to temporarily move to these places. This is a matter of saving lives, and the purpose of religious organizations is to save people, so they will naturally be happy to allow disaster victims to be temporarily resettled. After that, the nearby charitable organizations will be responsible for relief work. Those with a way to make a living will be allowed to find a way to make a living freely. Otherwise, further plans will be made to resettle them in the Northeast, Northwest, and other places to engage in reclamation, and this can also be used to investigate the population and food issues in the interior. (2) Rent large and small civilian boats to quickly go to the disaster area to rescue the disaster victims. For example, the water in Hankou is dozens of feet deep, and the Jiang and Han rivers have merged into one. The disaster victims have no way to escape and are waiting to die, but they cannot fly across the vast ocean. Therefore, rescuing the disaster victims is not only to relieve the immediate urgency, but also to reduce the burden of future relief. As for the shelters after the rescue, the local public security bureau should be responsible for protecting and maintaining order. (3) After the design committee discusses the fundraising work, it will be handed over to the fundraising committee for concrete implementation, and the press should be asked to encourage the public to voluntarily donate according to their ability. No matter how much is raised, it will supplement the failure to distribute donation forms widely. For those who voluntarily donate but have no way to pay, they can follow the example of the method used to raise funds for the Shaanxi disaster in Pingjin, where major newspapers in North China collect donations on behalf of the committee. The major newspapers in Shanghai should be asked to follow suit. If the newspapers are busy and do not have the time, then the committee will send a special commissioner to handle it, and the newspapers will announce the amount of donations every day. (4) The "Moving Troops to Fight the Flood" commentary in the Shen Bao on the 17th is extremely thorough. The committee should follow this principle and send a telegram to the authorities to earnestly adopt the suggestion to use troops other than those for suppressing bandits. (5) The current disaster situation is extremely serious, and the hidden dangers in the future are even more unthinkable. The committee should, based on the righteousness of pleading for the people, appeal to the Guangdong side to end the war as soon as possible, promote national unity, and work together to save this great calamity.

Trade Associations Should Be Responsible for Reporting the Sale of Japanese Goods

▲ Decision of the Inspection Committee of the Municipal Chamber of Commerce

▲ Anti-Japanese Association Warns Gantai Herbal Medicine Store

The Japanese Goods Inspection Committee of the Municipal Chamber of Commerce held a standing committee meeting yesterday and decided to send a letter to each trade association to be responsible for reporting the sale of Japanese goods by fellow traders. In addition, the Anti-Japanese Association sent a letter to Gantai Store warning that it should not ship Japanese herbal medicines, which are abundant in our country, and asked the Consul General in Taipei for details as follows:

▲ Standing Committee of the Inspection Committee The Japanese Goods Inspection Committee of the Municipal Chamber of Commerce held its first standing committee meeting yesterday. Those present included Pan Yisan, Zhou Renqing, Shi Jiumao, Yu Yangzhou, Cheng Guichu, Yuan Hongjun, and Qiu Liangyu, etc. Ye Jiaxing chaired the meeting and discussed the following matters: (1) A letter from Yuanlai Store stating that more than 3,000 packages of Dutch potato flour have been seized by the Anti-Japanese Association and requesting that the matter be verified and a letter be sent to release the goods. It was resolved to recommend Gong Jingyan, a representative of the Southern Goods Industry, to investigate and report to the committee for verification. (2) The Research Association of Warehouse Goods submitted a request from the Herbal Medicine Association to exempt seven types of herbal medicine that are the main raw materials from boycotting. It was resolved to hand it over to the investigation team. (2) It was resolved to hold meetings once a week on Tuesday afternoons at 3 PM. (4) It was resolved to send a letter to the Municipal Chamber of Commerce requesting it to forward the letter to each trade association to be responsible for reporting the sale of Japanese goods by fellow traders. (5) It was decided to convene a meeting of the investigation team this Friday and a meeting of the review team this Saturday.

▲ Anti-Japanese Association Warns Gantai Store The Anti-Japanese Association sent a letter to Gantai Store yesterday, warning: "Dear Sirs, On August 8, we received your letter stating that the Japanese herbal medicine you purchased was still in Taiwan and had not been shipped. Fearing that the loading application would not be able to release the goods, the Sanda Trading Company specifically issued an official letter to the Consul General in Taipei for certification, requesting accommodation so that the goods could be shipped. After sending personnel to investigate, it was replied that the herbal medicines purchased were two types: pith and dendrobium. Our country's Sichuan and other provinces produce a lot of these and do not need to rely on Taiwan. At this time, the Japanese brutally killed overseas Chinese in Korea. All sectors of the city are facing a national crisis and the end is approaching, so they are strictly implementing economic severance with Japan and fighting for survival. As a fellow countryman, you should be working hard and sharing trials and tribulations together to resist foreign aggression. However, the store is not planning to do this and is shipping Japanese goods, which are abundant in our country, and is willing to be the first to resist the anti-Japanese movement, which is extremely hateful. Furthermore, the Consul General in Taipei does not understand the truth and issued an official letter for certification, requesting accommodation, which is even more shocking. In addition to asking the Consul General in Taipei for details, we are giving you a warning that all ordered Japanese goods are not allowed to be shipped to Shanghai. Otherwise, they will be seized and dealt with severely. We hope you will think carefully and act accordingly, and do not wait until it is too late to regret. This is addressed to Gantai Store."

▲ Letter Questioning the Consul General in Taipei The association also sent a letter to the Consul General in Taipei, stating, "Dear Sirs, On August 8, we received a letter from Gantai Store in this city stating that the Japanese herbal medicine it ordered from Japan was still in Taiwan and had not been shipped. Fearing that the loading application would not be able to release the goods, the Dasan Trading Company specifically issued an official letter to the Consul General in Taipei for certification, requesting accommodation so that the goods could be shipped. After sending personnel to investigate, it was replied that the herbal medicines were two types: pith and dendrobium. Our country's Sichuan and other provinces produce a lot of these and do not need to rely on Taiwan. At a time when compatriots across the country are strictly implementing economic severance with Japan, the store is still reordering Japanese goods, which is extremely wrong. Furthermore, at this time when the Japanese brutally killed overseas Chinese in Korea, all those who hold diplomatic positions should be working hard and leading the people to insist on anti-Japanese resistance and resist foreign aggression. However, your Consul General is not planning to do this and is actually issuing official letters for certification, requesting accommodation for the shipment of Japanese goods, which is truly shocking. Unless you have other intentions, there is no way to explain it. This has been proposed and recorded by the 11th standing committee meeting of the association. In addition to strictly warning Gantai Store that the goods are not allowed to be shipped to Shanghai, a corresponding letter of questioning is prepared. We hope that you will investigate and reply quickly. This is addressed to the Consul General in Taipei."

Municipal Finance Bureau's July Revenue

▲ Also Increased Compared to the Same Month Last Year

The Municipal Finance Bureau has recently seen a sharp increase in the amount of donations and taxes collected from various direct income sources, as previously reported. It has been learned that the bureau yesterday announced the revenue figures for October (July). Property tax amounted to $186,535.97, an increase of over $13,000 compared to the same month last year. Business tax was $32,412.35, a significant increase of over $32,000. License tax was $244,638.71, also an increase of approximately $44,000. Other items experienced varying degrees of increase or decrease, with a total increase of approximately $20,000. The total revenue was $462,826.27, an increase of $80,444.90 compared to the same month last year.

Local News Two

Cunning American Youth

▲ Recklessly Signing Bad Checks

▲ Exposure Occurred on the Ship

▲ Eventually Escaped and Stayed in Shanghai

According to the Continental Daily News, an American youth recently arrived in Shanghai by ship from Honolulu. After the ship sailed, he requested a first-class cabin from the purser, claiming to be a lawyer with an urgent case to handle in Manila, which was why he had made the trip so hastily without purchasing a ticket. The purser provided him with a luxurious cabin, filled out a ticket, and requested payment. The youth signed a check. When he was informed that the company's policy did not allow for accepting checks at that time, he claimed to have no cash. The ship owner then sent a wireless message to the drawee bank, only to find out that the youth not only had no funds but was also being investigated for repeatedly signing bad checks. The ship owner then detained him on the ship and brought him to Shanghai. Upon arriving in Shanghai, the youth claimed to have friends at the consulate who could provide assistance and insisted on going ashore. The ship owner refused, and sent him to the company's ship bound for the United States for deportation. This ship was scheduled to set sail in an hour, and those on both ships thought nothing more would happen. However, after the ship weighed anchor and left the shore, a headcount revealed that the youth had disappeared. The ship owner happened to glance back and saw him climbing ashore via a sampan in the distance. Since the ship had already left the shore, he let the matter go. From then on, the youth began signing checks on a grand scale in Shanghai, buying fashionable clothes, staying at a large Western hotel, and socializing lavishly. Women were particularly fond of associating with him. The banks, seeing the drawee bank's endorsement on his passport, initially accepted his checks. Although they now suspected him, the creditors, thinking him to be a lawyer, dared not report him to the court. These checks have now been sent to the United States and are expected to be returned to Shanghai in a few weeks with "insufficient funds" stamped on them. If the youth reappears at that time, he will be caught in the legal net and imprisoned. It is also rumored that he never set foot in the American Consulate in Shanghai, nor did he visit his friends.

Manager of Yongxing Exchange Shop Absconds with Huge Sum of Money

▲ Withdrew an Additional $40,000 Before Fleeing

▲ Arrested After Investigation

The Shanghai branch of the Yongxing Exchange Shop in Yingkou, Fengtian Province, was located at No. 6, Jiangxi Road, Sijing Road, Shanghai. Chen Xingwu from Fengtian was appointed as the manager. Since the beginning of this year, Chen had been embezzling funds, totaling more than $6,000. The head office learned of this and was planning to send someone to Shanghai to audit the accounts. Chen, upon hearing this news, secretly issued thirteen exchange bills, cashed them at various banks, and obtained 43,532.36 taels of silver before fleeing. When Liu Xuyuan, sent by the head office, arrived to audit the accounts, Chen had already fled. He reported the matter to the General Police Station. Chinese Detective Wen Da discovered that Chen had entrusted his friend Fan Jiesan to cash three of the exchange bills at the Bank of Communications. Fan was found at No. 365, Ningbo Road, and revealed that Chen was hiding at No. 8, Dabaoli, Avenue Bugeaud, French Concession. The detectives arrested Chen and learned that the embezzled funds had been deposited in various banks, and the deposit books were kept with his friend Zhao Xunting. The police then arrested Zhao and retrieved thirteen bankbooks, including: three accounts with Shanghai Bank, totaling $12,500; five accounts with the Four Banks Joint Savings Society, totaling $33,500; two accounts with the Donglai Bank, totaling $4,000; one account with the National Bank, totaling $4,000; and one account with the Hong Kong National Bank, totaling $5,500, for a total of $59,500. Chen Xingwu, Fan Jiesan, and Zhao Xunting were taken into custody. Yesterday morning, they were escorted to the First Special Court's Criminal Division One. Police lawyer Ru Baoyi explained the case and charged Chen Xingwu with embezzlement under Article 357 of the Criminal Code. He requested that Fan and Zhao be temporarily detained but not charged. Chen Xingwu fully confessed. Judge Cheng Shangfeng reviewed the confession and ordered the case to be adjourned for further hearing. Chen Xingwu was detained, while Fan Jiesan and Zhao Xunting were each released on bail of $3,000.

Municipal Finance Bureau Announces Measures for Citizens to Voluntarily Pay Property Tax

▲ Preferential Fees Will Be Issued

In order to improve the efficiency of property tax collection, the Municipal Finance Bureau has, in addition to continuing to handle matters according to regulations, formulated measures for citizens to voluntarily pay property tax and will issue preferential fees to encourage such payments. This matter has been submitted to and approved by the Municipal Government for trial implementation. It is reported that the bureau has decided to start the trial implementation in the Municipal Southern Tax Collection Office from this winter and will implement it citywide after successful results are achieved. The bureau announced the measures for citizens to voluntarily pay property tax yesterday. They are recorded as follows:

▲ Measures for Citizens to Voluntarily Pay Property Tax (1) All commercial and residential households in the city that voluntarily pay their quarterly property tax to the tax collection office in charge before the 10th of the first month of the quarter will receive a preferential fee of 2% of the amount paid (i.e., $2 per $100). (Note) Regardless of whether it is the owner or the tenant who pays the full amount of property tax to the tax collection office in charge, the entire preferential fee will be enjoyed by the payer. (2) If the payment is made after the deadline specified in the previous article, even if it is a voluntary payment, the right to enjoy the preferential fee will be forfeited. (3) Those who voluntarily pay property tax must pay the owner's donation and the tenant's donation at the same time and present the donation ticket from the previous quarter. After verification, the receipt for the current quarter's property tax will be issued together. (4) The receipt for voluntary property tax payment consists of five copies. The first and second copies will be issued to the payer. The third copy will be the property tax deduction certificate. The fourth copy will be submitted for verification, and the fifth copy will be retained as a record. (Note) When issuing the preferential fee, the payer must sign and affix a seal on the property tax deduction certificate for verification purposes. (5) Households whose property tax is collected by the bureau's collectors at their doorsteps, even if it is before the 10th of the first month of the quarter, will not receive the preferential fee.

Shanghai Municipality Standard Clock Damage Compensation Measures

▲ Regardless of Intentional or Unintentional

▲ Compensation Must Be Made at the Original Price

The electrical standard clocks set up by the Municipal Bureau of Public Utilities have already begun to be installed. Fifteen clocks in South Shanghai and five clocks in Zhabei will soon be completed and put into use. The bureau has installed these standard clocks in busy city streets to benefit the public, making them easily susceptible to damage. Therefore, it has been approved by the Municipal Government to issue the Shanghai Standard Clock Damage Compensation Measures as follows: 1. Anyone who damages the municipality-owned electric clocks or their accessories (clock posts and attached advertisements, etc.), regardless of whether it is intentional or unintentional, shall be compensated according to these measures. 2. Anyone who damages the standard clocks or their accessories shall, in addition to being punished according to the Police Penalty Law, also be liable for repair and compensation. 3. If the damage is minor and can be repaired, the Bureau of Public Utilities will arrange for repairs, and all costs shall be borne by the person who caused the damage. 4. If the damage is serious and requires partial or complete replacement, the Bureau of Public Utilities will order the person who caused the damage to compensate at the current market price. 5. If the person who caused the damage wishes to replace the damaged parts themselves, they must first pay a corresponding deposit to the Bureau of Public Utilities and replace the parts according to the original standard clock brand and style, and restore them to their original state within the time limit set by the Bureau of Public Utilities. After the inspection and approval by the Bureau of Public Utilities, the deposit will be refunded. If the deadline is exceeded, the deposit will be confiscated as compensation. 6. If the damage affects the municipality-owned electric clock lines, the person who caused the damage shall be responsible for compensating all losses.

Forging Public Works Department Garbage Disposal Certificates

People's hearts are not as they used to be, and social customs are declining. Fraudulent tricks are becoming increasingly bizarre. Ji Shixiang, a Jiangbei native who lives in Zhoujiaqiao, West Shanghai, is fifty-five years old and has been working in factories. Recently, he suddenly had an idea and colluded with someone named Cai to privately mint a large number of copper tokens engraved with the words "British Concession Public Works Department Health Bureau No.□□ Garbage Disposal Certificate." The tokens were circular, about the size of a large silver dollar. The other day, Ji took several of these copper tokens and told Xu Sihe (48 years old) from Gaoyou and Zhu Lifu (25 years old) from Yancheng, who worked at the Toyota factory, that the Public Works Department Health Office now needed to hire a large number of garbage collectors. His friend Cai had obtained a large number of copper token certificates and if they were willing to take on this role, the monthly salary would be very high, costing a number of dollars per token. Xu and Zhu, hearing this, thought it was better than working in the factory and were naturally happy to do so. They discussed it with each other and, fearing that the copper token was forged by Ji to defraud them, decided to wait until the next day to make a decision. Yesterday, Xu and Zhu took the copper token and went to the Public Works Department Health Office to inquire about its authenticity. The office received the copper token and knew that it was a fake used for extortion. They sent Xu and Zhu to the Harbin Police Station for investigation. The police chief sent Chinese detective Yan Shiqing to transfer Xu and Zhu to the Sixth District Police Station in West Shanghai for questioning. The police station then sent police officers to the address to arrest Ji Shixiang and seized nineteen newly made identical copper tokens. After questioning them separately, District Chief Ren learned that Ji claimed that he did not know that the copper tokens were fake and that Cai had entrusted him with them. He ordered that Ji be temporarily detained for further investigation.

Business License Exempted from Stamp Tax

▲ Approved by the Ministry of Finance to the National Federation of Commerce

The National Federation of Commerce yesterday telegraphed to all chambers of commerce in the country that the Hunan Provincial Federation of Commerce had previously sent a letter requesting the transfer of the abolition of stamp tax on business licenses. The federation then telegraphed to the Ministry of Finance, requesting the withdrawal of the order. On August 15th of this year, the Ministry of Finance issued an approval letter No. 13482 stating: "I have received your telegram. After investigation, the collection of business tax in various provinces was originally determined to issue business licenses, which are the same as the business licenses stipulated in Articles 2, Class 3, Nos. 31, 33, and 34 of the Stamp Tax Regulations. Stamp tax should be collected accordingly. We have approved the tiered stamp tax collection method and ordered compliance. Subsequently, the Business Tax Law was officially promulgated on June 13th of this year. The business license has been changed to a business survey certificate. After detailed interpretation of the legal intent, the certificate permitting merchants to operate has been changed to the basis for public investigation and taxation. It is fundamentally different from the nature of the business license in the regulations, and Article 3 of the same law stipulates that no certificate fee is collected for the business survey certificate, and no tax is collected. Since the method has been changed, the original plan for stamping is difficult to apply. The current business survey certificates are exempt from stamp tax to comply with the law. We have notified the stamp tax bureaus in various provinces to handle the certificates and licenses accordingly. I hereby inform you." The National Federation of Commerce Chairman Lin Kanghou, Standing Committee Members Su Minsheng Zhang Yuquan, Lu Guangxu, Chen Riping, Li Kuian, and Peng Chuli. (20) Print

Slaughter Improvement Funding Management Committee Rules

▲ City Government Revised and Promulgated

The City Government yesterday announced the revised rules of the City Slaughter Improvement Funding Management Committee as follows: Article 1. The Shanghai Municipal Government shall, from the slaughter tax revenue, allocate nine cents per slaughtered pig to be used as funds for various undertakings related to the improvement and organization of the meat industry, and establish a Management Committee (hereinafter referred to as the Committee) to manage it. Article 2. The duties of the Committee are as follows: 1. Matters concerning the safekeeping of funds; 2. Matters concerning the improvement of sanitation facilities in the fresh meat industry; 3. Matters concerning the improvement of slaughtering; 4. Other construction or public welfare matters concerning the fresh meat industry. Article 3. The Committee shall have a fixed number of seven members, organized by the following representatives: A. One representative from the Health Bureau; B. One representative from the Finance Bureau; C. One representative from the Social Affairs Bureau; D. One representative from the City Chamber of Commerce; E. Three representatives from the Fresh Meat Trade Association. Article 4. The members mentioned in the preceding article shall be appointed by their respective agencies or elected by their respective groups, and then submitted to the City Government for record. Article 5. The Committee shall have three standing committee members, and the representative of the Social Affairs Bureau shall be designated as the ex officio chairman of the committee. The remaining two shall be elected from among the committee members. Article 6. The Committee shall be attached to the Social Affairs Bureau. Regular meetings shall be held once a month, and ad hoc meetings shall be held irregularly, both of which shall be convened by the standing committee members. Article 7. These funds shall, from the date of collection of the slaughter tax in this city, be allocated monthly by the Finance Bureau to the Management Committee, which shall issue receipts. Article 8. These funds shall be designated for deposit in the Shanghai Municipal Bank. Article 9. The use of these funds shall not be paid without the resolution of the Committee and the approval of the City Government for record. Article 10. The Committee shall submit a report to the City Government every six months on the work of the Committee and the income and expenditure of funds, and shall also send a letter to relevant agencies and groups. Article 11. Detailed rules for the operation of the Committee shall be formulated separately. Article 12. If there are any matters not covered by these rules, they may be amended at any time. Article 13. These rules shall be implemented from the date of promulgation by the City Government.

▲ Because the Term of Lease Expired on September 24th

▲ Recently, Japanese Police Committed Assaults Again in Chongqing

The Sichuan Fellow-Provincials Association in Shanghai yesterday sent a telegram to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs regarding the issue of reclaiming the Japanese Concession in Chongqing, which read: "To Minister Wang of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs in Nanjing: We have learned that the term of lease for the Japanese Special Administrative Concession in Wangjiatuo, Chongqing, expired on September 24th of this year. Last month, this association telegraphed your ministry, requesting that it be reclaimed as scheduled. However, your ministry has yet to make any indication. Furthermore, according to reports from Chongqing, on [omitted] day of last month, the police officer of the concession, Odazawa, again committed assault while intoxicated, and groundlessly beat Qian Youyu, a worker at the Daxin Iron Factory, causing serious injuries. The people of Chongqing, enraged by righteous indignation, have organized an anti-Japanese assembly and are engaging in economic severance with Japan, and will not cease until the concession is reclaimed. Now, there are only a little over a month left until September 20th. What is your ministry's plan for this concession? Will you permit the Japanese to renew the lease? If so, your ministry's claim to reclaim concessions will lose its meaning. Will you proceed to reclaim it? Why is it that, with the matter imminent, no definite plan has been seen? Will it be indefinitely delayed and shelved like Lushun and Dalian? If this is what is meant by revolutionary diplomacy, then this association dares not obey the order. For the sake of safeguarding national territory and washing away the humiliation of the people of Sichuan, this association does not hesitate to take the liberty of again urging your ministry to implement the foreign policy of this party, respect the declaration of the National Assembly to abolish treaties, and promptly negotiate with the Japanese side to reclaim the concession on time, in order to comfort the hopes of the people of Sichuan. What should be done? We respectfully await your clear instructions. Sichuan Fellow-Provincials Association, respectfully."
